        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3069942191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7450782360932851966">This book really came at me unexpectedly. Going into this, I did not know that these characters and their stories would stick with me for days, weeks, after. Immediately after finishing this book, I felt like starting it all over again. <br/><br/>I think <i>Jellicoe Road</i> is best read if you jump into it blindly. So I'll try not to give too much away in this review. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“These people have history and I crave history. I crave someone knowing me so well that they can tell what I'm thinking.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Since the age of eve</span>
  <span id="freeText7450782360932851966" style="display:none">This book really came at me unexpectedly. Going into this, I did not know that these characters and their stories would stick with me for days, weeks, after. Immediately after finishing this book, I felt like starting it all over again. <br /><br />I think <i>Jellicoe Road</i> is best read if you jump into it blindly. So I'll try not to give too much away in this review. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>“These people have history and I crave history. I crave someone knowing me so well that they can tell what I'm thinking.”</i>
</b><br /><br />Since the age of even Taylor Markham has been at boarding school. At seventeen she is now the chosen leader of her school's underground activities and is in charge of how they proceed in the annual territory wars against the townies and visiting cadets. <br />Taylor's past is filled with abandonment, grief and pain. When her caretaker at school, Hannah, the only adult she trusts, leaves unexpectedly Taylor has a need to know where Hannah could be and in doing so also finds out other unexpected truths.<br /><br /><br />I know many people did not enjoy this book because of the writing style and the confusion of the first half. It's definitely not everyone's cup of tea. <b>But for me, it was perfection</b>. <br /><br />Yes it was confusing but I love figuring things out. We got passages set in the past, which didn't follow a proper time line. The mystery of not knowing what was going on or how things connected added to my enjoyment. I <i>needed</i> to know how everything fit.<br /><br /><blockquote>“As I walk back to the school on my own, I realise I'm crying. So I go back to the stories I've read about the five and I try to make sense of their lives because in making sense of theirs, I may understand mine.”</blockquote><br /><br />I really loved the setting. I have never read a book set in Australia before and it was super interesting to read about. This was set around Christmas time which is the summer holidays in Australia. I could totally relate to that as I too live in the southern hemisphere. <br /><br />I am surprised by how quickly I became attached to the characters. Those in the past and present. I wanted them to be happy, to confront their fears and to be together. <br /><br /><blockquote>“Because people with that much spirit frighten the hell out of me. They make me want to be a better person when I know it's not possible.”</blockquote><br /><br />The side characters were so well fleshed out. And I was just as invested in their stories as I was in Taylor's. Their character growth and development and their own struggles was so beautiful to read. Watching them become more to one another brought me such joy. <br /><br /><blockquote>“But grief makes a monster out of us sometimes . . . and sometimes you say and do things to the people you love that you can't forgive yourself for.”</blockquote><br /><br /><br />This is a book that I will reread again and again and <i>know</i> that eveytime it will still impact me as it did the first time I read it. <br /><br />I think what also added to my experience was that I read this with a group of besties. We'd text eachother our thoughts and laugh about how much this book was making us cry. I had the best time reading this. A thousand thanks to Fares for suggesting we read one of his favourite books. It has become one of mine as well 🌻. <br /><br /><blockquote>“A home to come back to every day of their lives.<br />Where they would all belong or long to be.<br />A place on the Jellicoe Road.”</blockquote><br /><br />Buddy read with these lovelies 👉 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/30036082-warda" rel="nofollow noopener">Warda</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/36097076-t-rkan" rel="nofollow noopener">Türkan</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/58818027" rel="nofollow noopener">Fares</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42944800-karima-chermiti" rel="nofollow noopener">Karima</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7450782360932851966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_125606929" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125606929" />
    <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club"><img alt="Stacia (the 2010 club)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417661051p2/4013351.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125606929?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacia (the 2010 club)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacia (the 2010 club)" href="/user/show/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club">Stacia (the 2010 club)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=made-me-emotional">made-me-emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=realistic-general-or-lit-fiction">realistic-general-or-lit-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013351-stacia-the-2010-club?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125606929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer449097732761337889">Simply incredible. I cried way too much, but it was so worth it. Will review tomorrow when I can wrap my head around what to write.<br/><br/>*moves ahead a day in time*<br/><br/>After sleeping on it, I'm still struggling with how to write a proper review. There are some books which are virtually impossible to explain, and this is one of them. The GR book summary gives no indication what the book is really about, and truth be told, I'm not sure you'd want to know what the book is about before reading it.<br/><br/>The first 15</span>
  <span id="freeText449097732761337889" style="display:none">Simply incredible. I cried way too much, but it was so worth it. Will review tomorrow when I can wrap my head around what to write.<br /><br />*moves ahead a day in time*<br /><br />After sleeping on it, I'm still struggling with how to write a proper review. There are some books which are virtually impossible to explain, and this is one of them. The GR book summary gives no indication what the book is really about, and truth be told, I'm not sure you'd want to know what the book is about before reading it.<br /><br />The first 150 pages or so are completely frustrating and confusing. I knew this ahead of time, but I also knew that just about every single person who has read this has said the <i>exact</i> same thing, yet still gave the book 5 stars. There is a reason for this. The first part of the book is only giving you glimpses of the player's lives and their world. It almost reminded me of one of those movies that you watch in reverse, where the ending is the beginning and the beginning is the end - yet not quite. <br /><br />All I can do is echo the voices of those who prodded me to read the book - DON'T GIVE UP. You will not forget this book. You will not regret reading. It is so worth the read. Keep some tissues handy.<br /><br />As the story unfolds, the author starts giving us a crumb of information, then another, then another. Slowly the pieces of a broken story come together as one revelation follows another in a wave - a very emotional wave at that. Just when you think you've heard it all, more starts to come. Then more, then more. <br /><br />Pay attention to every single character. Just about every person's life is intertwined with the other characters in this story.<br /><br />I'm done trying to prod you to read this. Just read it. You will not be sorry for making the effort. Please, I beg you...battle through the first part of the book (which is confusing) until you get to the part that starts to get into your soul. Let's call this a dare. I have yet to find one person who did not love this book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="449097732761337889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/139160745?book_show_action=true">Jan 07, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer139160745" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5872496810515984553">Update 2020: No words are enough to express my love for this author! I bow to you, Melina Marchetta! When I grow up, I want to be you! (Ok, I might have lost that chance, maybe in a new life then, lol)<br/>__________________<br/><br/><b>Full (former) review:</b><br/><br/>It took me 113 days to write a full review.. I counted.<br/><br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-on-the-jellicoe-road-re-read.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380343645i/698962.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Reading one of Marchetta’s stories should be one of the <i>“10 things to do in your lifetime”</i>. Seriously, this woman is one of the most creative people alive, one of the most amazing writers I came across</span>
  <span id="freeText5872496810515984553" style="display:none">Update 2020: No words are enough to express my love for this author! I bow to you, Melina Marchetta! When I grow up, I want to be you! (Ok, I might have lost that chance, maybe in a new life then, lol)<br>__________________<br><br><b>Full (former) review:</b><br><br>It took me 113 days to write a full review.. I counted.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-on-the-jellicoe-road-re-read.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380343645i/698962.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Reading one of Marchetta’s stories should be one of the <i>“10 things to do in your lifetime”</i>. Seriously, this woman is one of the most creative people alive, one of the most amazing writers I came across and I wish I could put into words the awesomeness of this book, but I feel at a loss for words once more.<br><br>In fact, I should invent a new language with a dictionary full of ways to praise her talent.<br><br>Because Melina Marchetta doesn’t only write books, she creates entire worlds full of fleshed-out characters and shattering emotions, and after you read about them you feel like you’re the luckiest person in the known Universe and beyond. Because not many people in this world are able to feel what she makes you feel, and not many authors get to create such strong connections between the characters and the reader.<br><br>I feel like her stories have a soul. Like her characters are living beings trappend into a fantasy world, waiting for us to come and listen to their stories. They seem to breathe through our emotions, and I don’t remember a moment when I didn’t feel something (deep) towards this story and these wonderful characters.<br><br>Her words sing to me, they reach into the deep core of my own soul, they make me laugh through tears, they break my heart into thousand pieces but they also put it back in together, making it beat in a whole new rhythm, making it love and ache on a different level.<br><br>Once again, the complexity of the plot left me lightheaded, in awe, even though I knew what was coming my way. It’s been a while since the last time I read this book and I felt it all all over again: the confusion, the despair, the hope, the heartbreak, the happiness. My teary eyes could barely read and I was left breathless too many times to count. I loved EVERYTHING about this book, after all this time it is still my favorite story and I really hope that when (and if) you read this book you will be able to feel just a tiny-tiny part off all these blissful emotions flowing through my heart right now.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-on-the-jellicoe-road-re-read.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396288201i/9111564.jpg" width="405" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>THE STORY:<br><br>How much heartbreak can a heart take?<br><br>Jellicoe road is a roller coaster, a story meant to break hearts – one about true friendship and love, about forgiveness and salvation, about hope and disappointment, about life and death and everything in between.<br>It simply left me in awe again because there is no tiny detail, there is nothing less important in this story. Everything has value, all words have power – to make you laugh or cry, to dream and hope.. and the real beauty of it is connecting all the threads in this fabulous piece of art.<br><br>But as heartbreaking and intense as it might be, it is also fun, and I found myself smiling more than once. So don’t go thinking that this is a depressing book, it is not; it has the perfect balance between joy and sadness, between delight and heartbreak – but don’t believe me, see it for yourself!<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-on-the-jellicoe-road-re-read.html#chr" rel="nofollow noopener">THE CHARACTERS:</a><br><br>I can’t put into words how much compassion I felt towards <a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-on-the-jellicoe-road-re-read.html#chr" rel="nofollow noopener">the characters</a> in this story. I don’t think there’s one that didn’t leave an impression on me. Some times they made me laugh (even through tears), some other I just wanted to hold them close to my heart and protect them from all the hurt in their lives.<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-on-the-jellicoe-road-re-read.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1396288201i/9111565.jpg" width="405" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>CONCLUSION:<br><br>Every time I read “On the Jellicoe Road” it simply takes my breath away.<br>I fall in love with this book all over again, it hits me full strength no matter how well I think I know the story, it makes me smile and cry and sometimes both in the same time, all while I get drunk on the beauty of Marchetta’s words. Pure talent, pure Aussie awesomeness!<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-on-the-jellicoe-road-re-read.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334106i/693595.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>The full review can be found at: <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/melina-marchetta/review-on-the-jellicoe-road-re-read.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a> </i><br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br><br>Favourite quote (one of the many):<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/authors/melina-marchetta/review-on-the-jellicoe-road-re-read.html#favq" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1407410777i/10710234._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_146452913" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/146452913" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/146452913?book_show_action=true">Feb 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=the-real-5-star-deal">the-real-5-star-deal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-loved">books-i-loved</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer146452913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15216425442290411658">This book is so fucked up. Completely, totally fucked up. Everybody in it is fucked up, and living their lives is fucked up, and by the time you're done with it, you're fucked up, but you can't tell because your head is cloudy from all the tears you've shed getting through this fucked-up book. <br/><br/>I hate On The Jellicoe Road. I hate books that make me cry, and this book made me want to weep tears of blood for all that lost youth and promise, and the pain of loss and the promise of the future. If som</span>
  <span id="freeText15216425442290411658" style="display:none">This book is so fucked up. Completely, totally fucked up. Everybody in it is fucked up, and living their lives is fucked up, and by the time you're done with it, you're fucked up, but you can't tell because your head is cloudy from all the tears you've shed getting through this fucked-up book. <br /><br />I hate On The Jellicoe Road. I hate books that make me cry, and this book made me want to weep tears of blood for all that lost youth and promise, and the pain of loss and the promise of the future. If somebody had told me how mixed-up and emotional this book was going to make me feel, I would have abandoned it in a corner and floated off to the simple uncomplicated world of supernatural ass-kicking, where nobody dies and even if they do, they rarely stay dead. <br /><br />In the big debate of Saving Francesca versus Jellicoe Road, I would have to pick Jellicoe Road. I liked Francesca better, but that's because it made me laugh and think and smile mistily, but it never, ever, shoved me into the wringer and brought me out feeling like a limp dishcloth. It never made me feel that piercing tender pain you get when you think of things long past that can never be regained. It never made me feel like I was drowning in the lives of people who are so real, it's hard to believe they don't exist and haven't consumed your life. Jellicoe Road is a harsher, deeper read, the sandpaper to Francesca's paint peeler. <br /><br />Undeniably, the writing is brilliant. It's evocative and tender, it makes the emotions in each page almost tangible. The characters are drawn brilliantly too, and despite the fact that over half of the main cast wants to kill themselves at one point or the other, you cannot help but be drawn to them. I loved Taylor and Griggs and Santangelo and Raffy, but my heart got well and truly tangled up with Narnie and Webb and Judd and Tate and Fitz. It's for them that my heart broke, and shattered into a million pieces. The story is told largely from the perspective of Taylor, but it is the ghosts that predominate, that breathe life into the story, ironic as that sounds. <br /><br />This is not a book for people who want a straightforward love story with a dash of drama. This is for people who want to appreciate good writing, and don't mind losing a little bit of themselves between the covers of a book in the process. Oh man, this book is just so seriously Fucked. Up. And I would so totally KILL anyone who dissed it. Ever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15216425442290411658" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_102012272" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/102012272" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/102012272?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flannery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flannery" href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061431838" href="/book/show/2999475-jellicoe-road">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone looking for good YA</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Flannery by: </span>
      All my GR friends
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=kcls">kcls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=young-adult-teen">young-adult-teen</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=so-good-i-stayed-up-to-read-it">so-good-i-stayed-up-to-read-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=aussie-ya-is-the-cats-meow">aussie-ya-is-the-cats-meow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer102012272" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5199673798634183557">A lot of people think that Henry David Thoreau* went to Walden to live a solitary life. I felt like that until I actually went to Walden Pond. Imagine my surprise when some friends and I decided to go for a hike, go for a swim and check out the scenery--we left Boston around 9...and we got there by 9:30. Yeah right, HDT, I could live deliberately in the woods, too, if I knew my transcendentalist cronies would bring me a Cinnabon and some pumpkin ale once in awhile.** Nevertheless, Thoreau’s idea</span>
  <span id="freeText5199673798634183557" style="display:none">A lot of people think that Henry David Thoreau* went to Walden to live a solitary life. I felt like that until I actually went to Walden Pond. Imagine my surprise when some friends and I decided to go for a hike, go for a swim and check out the scenery--we left Boston around 9...and we got there by 9:30. Yeah right, HDT, I could live deliberately in the woods, too, if I knew my transcendentalist cronies would bring me a Cinnabon and some pumpkin ale once in awhile.** Nevertheless, Thoreau’s idea served as the inspiration for Yeats’ poem <a href="http://www.eecs.harvard.edu/~keith/poems/Innisfree.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Lake Isle of Innisfree</a>*** from which <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta" title="Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a> quotes in this novel. Yeats, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lake_Isle_of_Innisfree" rel="nofollow noopener">who looks a little like Kenneth from 30 Rock</a>, wrote about Innisfree because, to him, it served as an idyllic place where he could always go for peace and solitude. (I find it rather amusing that both Thoreau and Yeats wrote fascinating works about livin’ la vida simple that become so popular. <b>Lesson:</b> If you find a perfect place, KEEP IT TO YOURSELF)But Marchetta's magnificent storytelling was only enhanced by her reference to Yeats' poem. Instead of pounding quotations into your head, like a sad number of authors do, Marchetta only mentioned <i>Innisfree</i> once in passing...but it stuck with me through the rest of the book.<br /><br />I don’t want to go into the plot of this book too deeply, for the point I took away from the book is that we all have those idyllic places we go to in our minds. For some of the characters in this novel, their Innisfree was with family, or with their childhood friends, or even just spending time with one particular person. It doesn't have to be a place at all. No matter how far we get away from those memories, they are always all polished up in our minds like the Hope Diamond when we need to imagine a perfect place in time.<br /><br />Marchetta’s characters, as usual, were intriguing and fleshed out. It is constantly amazing to me that I can read a book and be unable to visualize even the protagonist, while this author is able to give me an extensive cast of characters and I feel like each one of them is someone I know. From Santangelo to Griggs to Raffy to the Brigadier, I understood where they were coming from and could reasonable predict what they would do in a situation. Very rarely was I frustrated with choices that characters made. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Though I wish Hannah and Jude got together earlier and that they had raised Taylor as mother and father. To deprive her of a childhood that could’ve been better than it was out of loyalty to Tate was, though perhaps understandable, still frustrating. Same for Jessa. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I also have no idea how Marchetta can make my heart hurt one moment and make me hysterically laugh the next.<br /><br />I must admit that the territory war aspect of the novel was not my favorite, though I understand its place in the overall story. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[When it all comes to a close, I wonder if next year’s students, Townies, and cadets will see fit to just share the area? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> The transfer back and forth between Taylor's present day and Hannah's story was rough for the first fourth or so of the book. If you try it and get stuck, please truck through it--it is so worth it.<br /><br />As I knock each of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9778918.Australische_Jugendliteratur_der_90er_Jahre__Untersuchungen_zu__Josy_sucht_Josy__von_Melina_Marchetta_und__Bis_dann__Simon__von_David_Hill" title="Australische Jugendliteratur der 90er Jahre. Untersuchungen zu &quot;Josy sucht Josy&quot; von Melina Marchetta und &quot;Bis dann, Simon&quot; von David Hill by Tobias Seitz" rel="nofollow noopener">Melina Marchetta</a>’s book off my to-be-read stack, I am a little more sad. When I’m done with them, how long will I have to wait for a new one?<br /><br />*The Wikipedia entry for HDT informs me that he wore a “neckbeard” for many years and insisted many women found it attractive. 1) I never knew that hideousness had a name; and 2) If you are a woman that finds a neckbeard attractive and we are friends on here, just go ahead and defriend me.<br /><br />**He was only 1.5 miles from his homeboy Emerson’s house.<br /><br />***This poem is the shit.<br /><br />EDIT: I listened to the first third or so of this book and read the rest in book form. The audiobook was great but I wanted to read it faster. The only negative for the audiobook was the annoying DMB-type music that played between every chapter and at the beginning and end of every disc.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5199673798634183557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1817943693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15011064770133985474"><b>Honest to God, I don't even know what the hell I read.</b><br/><br/>Before I begin, you'll realize I've referred to this book as JelliNOE Road. Because that's what is: A NO.<br/><br/>Don't ask me what this book is about, because 1) I don't know what it's about, and 2) I'd like to forget this book exists.<br/><br/>Thank you. <br/><br/>JelliNOE Road has been on my TBR for a while. I added it because <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508' rel='nofollow noopener'>MAYBELINE</a> adores it. I only decided to pick it up last week because May and I had a deal. She fulfilled her part of the deal and me reading thi</span>
  <span id="freeText15011064770133985474" style="display:none"><b>Honest to God, I don't even know what the hell I read.</b><br /><br />Before I begin, you'll realize I've referred to this book as JelliNOE Road. Because that's what is: A NO.<br /><br />Don't ask me what this book is about, because 1) I don't know what it's about, and 2) I'd like to forget this book exists.<br /><br />Thank you. <br /><br />JelliNOE Road has been on my TBR for a while. I added it because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508" rel="nofollow noopener">MAYBELINE</a> adores it. I only decided to pick it up last week because May and I had a deal. She fulfilled her part of the deal and me reading this book was fulfilling my part. LOOK HOW THAT TURNED OUT.<br /><br />If you love this book, I'm glad you did! But I highly doubt you want to continue reading this review.<br /><br />I'm aware I'm a minority here but I was literally <u>suffering</u> as I read this, because 1) Boring 2) Boring 3) Boring 4) Confusion level 10,000 6) HUH? 7) ????? 8) ?????, and 9) WHAT THE HELL IS GOING ON?<br /><br />Listen, I don't have a problem with confusing plots, as long as I <i>at least</i> get a <u>tiny bit of sense</u> of what's going on and it gets me hooked, but in JelliNOE Road... I don't even know, guys. NOPE. NOPE. NOPE. Literally, the only thing I can tell you about this book is what's written in the blurb and the characters' names. <br /><br />I started reading this book last week, but I was in a horrible slump, and apparently this book is not the best book to read during one. So, I stopped reading it for a few days while I fixed my slump. It was basically over beginning of this week and then I picked JelliNOE again two days ago. DID THINGS GET BETTER? NOPE.<br /><br />JelliNOOOOOOOOOE.<br /><br />Guys, please, someone tell me <b>what was happening in this book</b>. Why did everyone cry over it? What was the point? WHAT DID I MISS? This is actually stressful because I had high hopes???? <b>AND NOW I JUST WANT TO BUY A PHYSICAL COPY SO I CAN THROW IT OUT OF MY DAMN WINDOW.</b><br /><br />Also, ZERO connection with the characters (Jonah was okay, but whatever). Our MC, Taylor... Queen of Whining and Crying. That's her new name.<br /><br />In conclusion, JelliNOE Road is my first AND last book by Melina Marchetta.</span>

<div id="review_214600239" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/214600239" />
    <a title="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva"><img alt="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392555495p2/1491042.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/214600239?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aly (Fantasy4eva)" href="/user/show/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva">Aly (Fantasy4eva)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">THE WORLD</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aly (Fantasy4eva) by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/2619049-audrey">Audrey</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=hilarious">hilarious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=oh-how-the-heart-flutters">oh-how-the-heart-flutters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=my-kinda-protagonist">my-kinda-protagonist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=pleasantly-surprised">pleasantly-surprised</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=fast-paced-and-engrossing">fast-paced-and-engrossing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=digging-the-premise">digging-the-premise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=boys-that-make-me-swoon">boys-that-make-me-swoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1491042-aly-fantasy4eva?shelf=you-inspire-me">you-inspire-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer214600239" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12227893011369860597"> <b>“He’s the most beautiful creature I have ever seen and it’s not about his face, but the life force I can see in him. It’s the smile and the pure promise of everything he has to offer. Like he’s saying, ‘Here I am world, are you ready for so much passion and beauty and goodness and love and every other word that should be in the dictionary under the word life?’”</b><br/><br/>Sometimes, guys, simply reading a book once is not enough. <br/><br/>You find that reading it a second time offers you a whole other reading exper</span>
  <span id="freeText12227893011369860597" style="display:none"> <b>“He’s the most beautiful creature I have ever seen and it’s not about his face, but the life force I can see in him. It’s the smile and the pure promise of everything he has to offer. Like he’s saying, ‘Here I am world, are you ready for so much passion and beauty and goodness and love and every other word that should be in the dictionary under the word life?’”</b><br /><br />Sometimes, guys, simply reading a book once is not enough. <br /><br />You find that reading it a second time offers you a whole other reading experience. <br /><br />Those once slow 100 pages now whiz you by, and you realise it was not the pace that was at fault, but your confusion.<br /><br />You savour it so much more. Make sense of certain references - crush on the plot, characters and writing, and fall in love with Jonah Griggs all over again.<br /><br />It frustrates me so much to know that I can never do this book justice. That so many readers out there have yet to read this beauty. <br /><br />The thing is, somehow, even though I knew what was going to happen, I choked up and laughed like a mad women at the exact same scenes I did the first time around. What made me smile at times was how the little tissues were still there. So many times I would be about to bookmark a certain moment only to realise that it was already bookmarked. I suppose I know myself too well ;)<br /><br />When I approached the last 100 pages I decided to read them outside in the garden. I have never had that urge before, but It was dark outside, silent and soothing in a way that I couldn't imagine it being inside. It felt right to read those last pages alone - in a peaceful surrounding. Yet, like last time, I dreaded that last page, and when it had ended - I closed the book and just allowed my thoughts to take over and savour them, because I knew it would be a long time before any other book would ever make me feel like this again. I took that moment to mourn characters and a world I genuinely felt I had lost - taking some solace in the fact that I would return to them when the feeling of loss became close to unbearable.<br /><br />You know, I can see myself reading this every year, discovering something new every time, loving the characters even more - if that's even possible.<br /><br />Once again I was left with this undeniable ache that made me want to be a part of these characters lives, but I think what bothered me the most, and what really made me feel somewhat of a loss, was knowing that I will never know a Tate, Hannah, Webb, Jude, Fitz, Jonah, Ben, Raffy, Chaz, Jessa, and Taylor. <br /><br />I feel like I'm saying goodbye to something personal every time I turn over that last page, but now I know that's hardly the case. <br /><br />LOVE does not even come close to describing what I feel for this book <br /><br />Treasure it guys<br /><br />And then read it all over again &lt;3 </span>
  <a data-text-id="12227893011369860597" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_41542634" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/41542634" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1215148-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/41542634?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/1215148-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780061431838" href="/book/show/2999475-jellicoe-road">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1215148-emily?shelf=ya-childrens_lit">ya-childrens_lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1215148-emily?shelf=2008-cybils-finalists">2008-cybils-finalists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1215148-emily?shelf=2009-01">2009-01</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer41542634" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6818515870335580587">So I just don't get what others love about this book. It's a Cybil's Finalist and a ALA Printz Award Winner. So people LOVE Jellicoe Road and I usually follow popular librarian opinion, but I just can't get on this bandwagon.<br/><br/>I felt like the writing was very, very confusing. For the first 100 pages I really couldn't tell what was going on. Don't get me wrong - dramatic and interesting things were happening, but I couldn't even begin to see how they were related. The character development is very </span>
  <span id="freeText6818515870335580587" style="display:none">So I just don't get what others love about this book. It's a Cybil's Finalist and a ALA Printz Award Winner. So people LOVE Jellicoe Road and I usually follow popular librarian opinion, but I just can't get on this bandwagon.<br /><br />I felt like the writing was very, very confusing. For the first 100 pages I really couldn't tell what was going on. Don't get me wrong - dramatic and interesting things were happening, but I couldn't even begin to see how they were related. The character development is very spread out and most of the characters do not become clear until the end.<br /><br />There are two plot lines -<br /><br />1 - Taylor's life at Jellicoe School - The school has tradition of playing war games with the local townies and the cadets of a military school. They fight over territories, trails, and clubhouses. They take it very seriously, but it’s mostly in good fun. Taylor is the student leader of the Jellicoe School (like head girl - very big responsibility), but the school is made up of 6 houses and all of the houses have leaders too and they must collaborate to wage war against the townies and cadets.<br /><br />2 - Taylor's life before Jellicoe School – Taylor’s father has been killed and her mother is an abandoning drug addict. Taylor has no family to speak of but is taken care of by a local woman named Hannah. Hannah is writing a book about the goings on of Jellicoe School when she attended and Taylor is using the book to piece together her own random memories to understand what her life was actually about – mainly the story of her mother and father.<br /><br />In my opinion, these two plot lines do not mix. I didn’t know when to take Taylor seriously or when she was in deep emotional distress. One moment Taylor’s reclaiming territory for the Jellicoe School and the next moment she’s drowning a cat with her bare hands.<br /><br />There are very moving parts to this story. I felt for Taylor, Hannah, Griggs, &amp; Jude, but everyone beyond that didn’t touch me. They were just part of the confusion.<br /><br />Will someone please, please tell me what they LOVE about this book and what makes it a multiple award winner? Is something wrong with my logic? </span>
  <a data-text-id="6818515870335580587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_225396214" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/225396214" />
    <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely"><img alt="K.D. Absolutely" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471967140p2/2156200.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/225396214?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="K.D. Absolutely" class="user" itemprop="url" name="K.D. Absolutely" href="/user/show/2156200-k-d-absolutely">K.D. Absolutely</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061431852" href="/book/show/7042434-jellicoe-road">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to K.D. by: </span>
      GR-TFG 100 Favorite Books (2011 version)
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=tfg-100">tfg-100</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=populist">populist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=family-drama">family-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2156200-k-d-absolutely?shelf=trashy">trashy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer225396214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11023867499396066726">Every Filipino who loves his country must read this book.<br/><br/>Reason: On April 13, 2012, North Korea's long-range rocket launched, failed. <a href='http://www.reuters.com/article/2012/04/13/us-north-korea-rocket-idUSBRE83B1OR20120413' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reuters</a> is now saying that, embarrassed by rocket crash, North Korea may now be thinking of trying nuclear test. <br/><br/>Check the path and the trajectory plan of that failed rocket launch:<blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361574i/712586.jpg' width='400' height='300' alt='northkorea' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote>Do you see that tail-end of the yellow line? That's Luzon, the biggest island in the Philippines. That's where Manila is. That's where I live!<br/><br/>But why should we read this book?<br/><br/>Here's</span>
  <span id="freeText11023867499396066726" style="display:none">Every Filipino who loves his country must read this book.<br><br>Reason: On April 13, 2012, North Korea's long-range rocket launched, failed. <a href="http://www.reuters.com/article/2012/04/13/us-north-korea-rocket-idUSBRE83B1OR20120413" rel="nofollow noopener">Reuters</a> is now saying that, embarrassed by rocket crash, North Korea may now be thinking of trying nuclear test. <br><br>Check the path and the trajectory plan of that failed rocket launch:<blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361574i/712586.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="northkorea" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote>Do you see that tail-end of the yellow line? That's Luzon, the biggest island in the Philippines. That's where Manila is. That's where I live!<br><br>But why should we read this book?<br><br>Here's why:<blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380361574i/712587.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="president" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote>He reads this book!<br><br>Seriously, I am one of the moderators of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/480-the-filipino-group" rel="nofollow noopener">The Filipino Group</a> here in Goodreads. This book, <i>Jellicoe Road</i> by an Australian novelist, Melina Marchetta is our book of the month and we will have our face-to-face book discussion on Saturday. As a moderator and one of the senior members of the group, some members ask me what I think of the book. Even if they don't say or admit it, my views influence some of them. At this point, I guess my job is to encourage them to read the book and join the actual book discussion. That's why even if I did not like this book, I cannot rate this with 1 star. Why I did not like this book?<blockquote>1. I cannot understand why the first 100 pages should be made confusing<br>2. The claim or fight for territory has nothing to do with the rest of the book. Also, I do not understand exactly how it is supposed to work.<br>3. The love affair between Taylor and Briggs is too mushy for my taste. Felt like Katniss-Peeta or Bella-Edward. I'm too old for that.<br>4. Taylor is a pathetic female character IMO.<br>5. Taylor is asked to lead even if she is asthmatic. Is there nobody else who can lead?</blockquote>Anyway, according to my trusted friends in this group, the book is amazing. Maybe they are still young and the story "speaks" to them. So, let's leave it at that. However, I can say that this book has a good intent. It also has a developed story that other readers can emphatize with. I guess that this is just not for me. <br><br>But it is my ardent desire that this book will influence our North Korean friend to back off in his evil plan of building nuclear arsenal in the side of the world. Stop your expansionist plan, please and be content on what you have. Then if you have to test nukes, please don't point it to the Philippines! See, we also love Melina Marchetta! See, we both read and enjoy <i>this</i> book! <br><br>Thanks for lending me this book, Aaron.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1452829-mary-ravager-of-tomes?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1764588738" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12949071293309963526">This book was recommended to by the lovely <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508' rel='nofollow noopener'>MAYFLOWER</a>! And boy, do I have a lot of gratitude that she pulled this book to the forefront of my TBR list.<br/><br/>I'm gonna be honest, when I first started reading this I didn't find myself immediately drawn into the story. I was like that new kid in a group that's sort of hanging out on the edge of conversation, listening but not really participating.<br/><br/><u>But then I saw the light.</u><br/><br/>Things started to come together for me once Taylor began to pursue the truth of her p</span>
  <span id="freeText12949071293309963526" style="display:none">This book was recommended to by the lovely <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508" rel="nofollow noopener">MAYFLOWER</a>! And boy, do I have a lot of gratitude that she pulled this book to the forefront of my TBR list.<br /><br />I'm gonna be honest, when I first started reading this I didn't find myself immediately drawn into the story. I was like that new kid in a group that's sort of hanging out on the edge of conversation, listening but not really participating.<br /><br /><u>But then I saw the light.</u><br /><br />Things started to come together for me once Taylor began to pursue the truth of her past. But looking back, the beginning being on the slower side gave me a chance to get to know the characters and so I'm not going to say that it's a bad thing overall. <br /><br />It seems like the only other issue I had with this book could also be chalked up to personal preference and not something that's <i>objectively</i> wrong with the story. I just didn't love the setting of the Townies vs. Cadets vs. Students. Before things came into clearer focus I was thinking:<br /><br /><i>"What the fuck? People are actually getting hurt? These are school-aged kids? Whaaaat?"</i> But this setting does begin to feel much more appropriate once you get a bit further in.<br /><br /><b>God, everyone in this novel was so intense.</b><br /><br />Once I started realizing what was going on, who was who, and why certain things were relevant... Damn. My heart was beating so fast while making these discoveries, and they are all individually and <b>magnificently devastating.</b><br /><br />This is a book that slowly sinks its claws into you, and before you know it you're caught. <i>And once you're caught, there's no getting out until the end.</i><br /><br />The end broke my heart into so many pieces. I'm still picking them up. Such a wonderfully genuine and heartfelt story, with characters that come walking right out of the pages to meet you. This book is an intricately woven web of love and tragedy.<br /><br />I'm so glad that I've read this, and I feel it will have an impact on me long after I write this review.</span>

        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1087757222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10668689311354666745"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424871701i/13812595._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>☠ <b>Territorial War buddy read/reread with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please' rel='nofollow noopener'>Chelsea</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11285518-jennifer' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jennifer</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/28353412-jen' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jen</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17688793-laura' rel='nofollow noopener'>Laura</a> & <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/18516120-harriet' rel='nofollow noopener'>Harriet</a></b> ☠<br/><br/><b>What happens when you reread this incredible book?</b> <i>What? You fucking cry, what do you think?</i><br/><br/><i>Well, you have seen me <s>gushing frantically</s> obsessing over this book for a while now, so you know you have to brace yourself because this book? <b>It possibly became my favorite. Ever.</b> That kind of means something when we read a million book a year, right?</i> <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>"I fall in love with these kids over and over again and my heart aches</b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText10668689311354666745" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424871701i/13812595._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>☠ <b>Territorial War buddy read/reread with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please" rel="nofollow noopener">Chelsea</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/11285518-jennifer" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/28353412-jen" rel="nofollow noopener">Jen</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/17688793-laura" rel="nofollow noopener">Laura</a> &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/18516120-harriet" rel="nofollow noopener">Harriet</a></b> ☠<br><br><b>What happens when you reread this incredible book?</b> <i>What? You fucking cry, what do you think?</i><br><br><i>Well, you have seen me <s>gushing frantically</s> obsessing over this book for a while now, so you know you have to brace yourself because this book? <b>It possibly became my favorite. Ever.</b> That kind of means something when we read a million book a year, right?</i> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I fall in love with these kids over and over again and my heart aches for their tragedies and marvels at their friendship".</b>
</blockquote> <br>▒ <b>This book. This <i>fucking</i> BOOK.</b> ▒<br><br>Why is it so <i>special</i> to me? You mean, except from the fact it's written by Marchetta and contains Jonah Griggs in it? Apart from that? <br><br>Well, what you need to know is that <b>few authors manage to change my perception of myself as a reader.</b> <br><br>Yet if there's something I learnt this year, that's Melina Marchetta's books are written in a way that makes me want to create a stamp which would say - <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414332878i/11641171._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That says it all. The reason I rarely cry when I read is the fact <b>I hate feeling manipulated</b>. I loathe it when I can see through the author's intentions and I'm pretty sure that's why I never succeeded in finishing <i>The fault in our stars</i>. Melina Marchetta's books show me something I was eager to learn, because even if I knew it deep down inside, I was seeking out the moment I'd unravel all my doubts : <b>No, I'm not a cold-hearted reader.</b> <br><br>I was just longing for stories which really speak to me, because, never, <i>ever</i> again I want to find myself thinking <i>'oh, I think I'm supposed to cry right now'</i>. The beauty of her books lies in the <b>surprise</b> <u>they never fail to create in me</u> : I could express it with a single word : <b>suddenly</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414332878i/11641172._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And <i>that emergence of unexpected feelings?</i> <b>I live for that shit</b>. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414332878i/11641173._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>▒ <b> But this book. This <i>fucking</i> BOOK.</b> ▒<br><br><i>Jellicoe road</i> takes us into the life of characters so strongly convinced of the uselessness of their life that we want to fight for them. We want to tear the appearances out, and above all that, we're grateful to Melina Marchetta because her characters are so relatable and real that <b>we can find pieces of ourselves in them</b>. Pieces of our friends. Pieces of our family. Pieces of my heart that broke for Jonah Griggs <i>over and over again</i>. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Please don’t be crazy, Taylor,” Griggs whispers, leaning his head against mine. “Please don’t be crazy.” He kisses me, holding my face between his hands, whispering over and over again, <i>“Please"</i>.</b>
</blockquote> <br>Therefore don't worry if you're confused throughout the 100 first pages, I swear to you, there must surely come a stage when you'll find yourself utterly captivated by Taylor's journey. Moreover, after reading it a second time, I can assure you that this experience was even more emotional and that <b>Marchetta wrapped her plot brilliantly</b> - I noticed some things I couldn't see the first time and <i>WOW</i>. Just <i>WOW</i>. This structure? Incredible. Everything has a sense. Everything has a purpose. Nothing's useless. <b>Nothing</b>. <br><br>▒ <b> But this book. This <i>fucking</i> BOOK.</b> ▒<br><br><b>This is a tale about where we belong</b>. Is it a place? Is it a person? Is it <b>love</b>? <br><br><b>Can we stop belonging somewhere?</b> <br><br>Can we earn the right to belong or is it something we have in our heart <i>no matter what we do</i>? <br><br>Can we allow somebody else to be our <i>everything</i>? Because what happens, I'm asking I'm yelling, <b>what happens if our everything disappears?</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425339633i/13878952._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>*whisper*</b> Do we disappear as well?<br><br>Now, I don't want to scare you <s>how that's too late?</s> and I can assure you that <i>Jellicoe Road</i> isn't the kind of book that makes your eyes ache all long without never releasing the tension. No. <b>That's just life, you know?</b> So prepare yourself for a ride - you're going to laugh, to be pissed, to be desperate at times, to lose hope and then fight to find it again - <br><br>You're going to live and feel and smile. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"Go on, admit it. When he hits the ground and the blood went flying and you knew in your heart his nose was broken, didn't you just want to jump for joy and stomp on his ugly face?"</b>
</blockquote><br>▒ <b> But this book. This <i>fucking</i> BOOK.</b> ▒<br><br>I don't want to talk about the plot. Damn, I just can't and I'll say only one thing : even if I guessed some parts of the mystery pretty fast, following Taylor and Jonah was an experience I'd have been sad to miss and <b>that captivating and splendorous story will linger in my heart and in my thoughts</b> for a very long time.<br><br><b>
  <u>You know what you have to do.</u>
</b> <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I reach the bottom and smash into him with my fists as hard as I can. He falls and I can't believe he goes down that easy, caught off balance.<br>"You care about nothing, you piece of shit!"<br>I'm on the verge of tears, like I always seem to be these days, and I hear the catch in my voice and I hate myself for it. He throws me off him and I can tell there is a fury in him.<br>"Never," he tells me in a tone full of ice, "under-estimate who or what I care for.”</b>
</blockquote><br><b>PS</b> : I have a million quotes to write, a million stories about Jonah, Webbs, Tate, Narny, Jude, Fitz, Taylor, Jessa to tell. But I won't. I won't because this is a book which must be savored blind. I won't even if Jonah Griggs is certainly one of the characters I will never forget. Just meet them, and if that's already the case, go reread it. That's even better the second time around, trust me. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437141825i/15542036._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_106103828" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/106103828" />
    <a title="Nomes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes"><img alt="Nomes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499148999p2/3842653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/106103828?book_show_action=true">Jun 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nomes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nomes" href="/user/show/3842653-nomes">Nomes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=aussie-ya">aussie-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=shining-with-genius-like-brilliance">shining-with-genius-like-brilliance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=faves-of-faves">faves-of-faves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=books-that-linger">books-that-linger</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=powerful-impact">powerful-impact</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=swoon">swoon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=tissue-box-books">tissue-box-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=love-the-premise">love-the-premise</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=my-kind-of-awesome">my-kind-of-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3842653-nomes?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer106103828" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6505908903419271510">I first read 'On The Jellicoe Road' in 2006. I had been DYING for it's release ~ and can still remember how tingly and giddy I felt as I walked home with my copy. Back then, I had 3 kids under 5 and couldn't wait for them to get in bed so I could curl up and savour my new Melina Marchetta.<br/><br/>On The Jellicoe Road is notorious for people finding the beginning confusing ~ and I have seen lovers of the book urge people to persevere to find it's magic. <br/><br/>It was not like that for me. From the first chapter</span>
  <span id="freeText6505908903419271510" style="display:none">I first read 'On The Jellicoe Road' in 2006. I had been DYING for it's release ~ and can still remember how tingly and giddy I felt as I walked home with my copy. Back then, I had 3 kids under 5 and couldn't wait for them to get in bed so I could curl up and savour my new Melina Marchetta.<br /><br />On The Jellicoe Road is notorious for people finding the beginning confusing ~ and I have seen lovers of the book urge people to persevere to find it's magic. <br /><br />It was not like that for me. From the first chapter ~ I was spellbound. I remember thinking it was beautiful and haunting and funny and so entirely utterly appealing ~ the prose and the mystery and the characters. I guess I did feel a little like: what is going on? But not in a distracting way. It was absorbing and engaging and mesmerising. And entirely unexpected.<br /><br />I LOVED how gorgeously chaotic the story initially felt. I knew NOTHING about it ~ I even wondered if Santangelo would be the love interest in the early days (which quickly flew from my mind as Jonah's (JONAH!) story started unravelling).<br /><br />I LOVE that I knew nothing about it. Not one review, not one opinion. I had my expectations of awesomeness (it was, after all, a Melina Marchetta and I had read (and re-read) her previous two books countless times. <br /><br />Reading it blindly was a stunning experience: I felt like the whole world was just me and the book. That the entire experience was mine. That no one had gone before me. That the story was for me and I was a part of the story. I still feel like that, in a way. I see others discovering it and loving it and I am SO proud of it (as if, somehow, it is mine, haha) ~ but a small part of me feels like it belongs uniquely to me. More to me than anyone else (I know this is a ridiculous sentiment, but I still feel it). I almost feel private about it ~ as if it has become a part of me and talking about is like letting others peek into my soul.<br /><br />That very first time: I read it all in one go. I was shattered and absorbed and breathless and incredulous. I fell in love with the characters and the prose and the setting. I still recall finishing the book and how I felt gutted and euphoric and in awe all at once. Too stunned to cry (even though it would have been lovely to weep), I lay in my bed for an hour, just thinking about it. And then ... I picked it up and started reading it from the beginning all over again. <br /><br />Since then, I have read it every year (sometimes more than once). It has never lost it's magic. It weaves itself deeper into me. It is my own personal cult book &lt;3<br /><br />It seems ridiculous that I have not reviewed my favourite book of all time. I think I just feel entirely too inadequate to be up the the task. I also feel like it is such a part of me that I want to hold it close and not share it with the world. Yet another part of me feels like I could talk about it all day long and never tire of things to say and quotes to quote. <br /><br />This isn't a review, per se. <br /><br />It is me, humbly telling you, that 'On The Jellicoe Road' is my favourite book of all time. It is brilliant and hopeful and ache-y and truly soul-changing. It is the kind of chaotically gorgeous masterpiece that you only ever-so-rarely stumble across. It is perfect in it's brilliance. It radiates life and hope even as it is filled with grief and sorrow. It is everything, <i> everything </i>, I love about reading, in such a way that it almost ruined me for other books ;) I am completely undone for it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6505908903419271510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/94655466?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2010</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061431852" href="/book/show/7042434-jellicoe-road">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3455554-janina?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer94655466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7301212583157957182">I’m at a loss for words. This book has made me cry and laugh out loud. It has made me fall in love with its characters, no matter how small their role. It is a book that I’m not likely to forget at any time. <br/><br/><b>Jellicoe Road</b> deals with death and loss, with abandonment, drug-addiction and suicide. Each character has her or his own terrible past to come to terms with, and sometimes I wondered: How do these people manage to live on when even I almost can’t cope with what they’ve been through? <br/>But abov</span>
  <span id="freeText7301212583157957182" style="display:none">I’m at a loss for words. This book has made me cry and laugh out loud. It has made me fall in love with its characters, no matter how small their role. It is a book that I’m not likely to forget at any time. <br /><br /><b>Jellicoe Road</b> deals with death and loss, with abandonment, drug-addiction and suicide. Each character has her or his own terrible past to come to terms with, and sometimes I wondered: How do these people manage to live on when even I almost can’t cope with what they’ve been through? <br />But above all, <b>Jellicoe Road</b> is a book about forgiveness and moving on, and about the love and friendship that helps you on this journey. As, beautifully said: <i>"What's the difference between a trip and a journey? [...] When we get there, you'll understand."</i><br /><br />Side note: If you are contemplating giving up on this book after about 100 pages, <b>don’t do it</b>. Even though I loved this story right from the start, I have heard from so many people who struggled. I can understand that the beginning may seem a little confusing with its eerie, almost dream-like quality, but it’s definitely worth reading on.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7301212583157957182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_8079815'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8079815-good-oil"><img alt="Good Oil" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1298925793l/8079815._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BQcn8Py4CYzPRRytlp2stHIbySkGLtGa2SrJ0RhJ+rJ1WkHAHkartXogIvignKZ6I3UjP2dCmN0WVAR5h7CTAw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta">About Melina Marchetta</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1277655889p3/47104.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/47104.Melina_Marchetta">Melina Marchetta
</a></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15897884538953371215">Melina Marchetta was born in Sydney Australia. Her first novel, Looking For Alibrandi was awarded the Children's Book Council of Australia award in 1993 and her second novel, Saving Francesca won the same award in 2004. Looking For Alibrandi was made into a major film in 2000 and won the Australian Film Institute Award for best Film and best adapted screen play, also written by the author. On the </span>
  <span id="freeText15897884538953371215" style="display:none">Melina Marchetta was born in Sydney Australia. Her first novel, Looking For Alibrandi was awarded the Children's Book Council of Australia award in 1993 and her second novel, Saving Francesca won the same award in 2004. Looking For Alibrandi was made into a major film in 2000 and won the Australian Film Institute Award for best Film and best adapted screen play, also written by the author. On the Jellicoe Road was released in 2006 and won the US Printz Medal in 2009 for excellence in YA literature. This was followed up by Finnikin of the Rock in 2008 which won the Aurealis Award for YA fantasy, The Piper's Son in 2010 which was shortlisted for the Qld Premier's Lit Award, NSW Premier's Lit Award, Prime Minister's Literary Awards, CBC awards and longlisted for the Miles Franklin Award. Her follow up to Finnikin, Froi of the Exiles and Quintana of Charyn were released in 2012 and 2013. Her latest novel Tell the Truth, Shame the Devil is an adult crime novel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15897884538953371215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
